  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7d69935f-484c-4a48-b5a4-616b5ee44ead'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText12315306763322106462" style="display:none"><i>You go through life thinking there’s so much you need…<br /><br />Until you leave with only your phone, your wallet, and a picture of your mother.</i><br /> <br />Marin hasn’t spoken to anyone from her old life since the day she left everything behind. No one knows the truth about those final weeks. Not even her best friend, Mabel. But even thousands of miles away from the California coast, at college in New York, Marin still feels the pull of the life and tragedy she’s tried to outrun. Now, months later, alone in an emptied dorm for winter break, Marin waits. Mabel is coming to visit, and Marin will be forced to face everything that’s been left unsaid and finally confront the loneliness that has made a home in her heart.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1902616805?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1902616805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1383087927634871731">This is the kind of book I want to write. Which is a pretty big thing to say, I suppose.<br/><br/>What I really appreciated was that Nina LaCour abandoned the idea that a novel has to be entirely plot driven. This is a book about relationships and emotions and I liked being caught up in Marin's brain. I loved that it took place in winter, on an abandoned university campus, where everything amplified Marin's feelings of emptiness and isolation. I like that things like being coloured or queer were present b</span>
  <span id="freeText1383087927634871731" style="display:none">This is the kind of book I want to write. Which is a pretty big thing to say, I suppose.<br /><br />What I really appreciated was that Nina LaCour abandoned the idea that a novel has to be entirely plot driven. This is a book about relationships and emotions and I liked being caught up in Marin's brain. I loved that it took place in winter, on an abandoned university campus, where everything amplified Marin's feelings of emptiness and isolation. I like that things like being coloured or queer were present but not plot devices. It all felt real and relevant. I also, and I cannot emphasize this enough, loved Nina LaCour's use of technology. I've made a video all about this, but I'm really irked by teenager representation that doesn't involve the internet or cellphones. Here it was masterfully intertwined. It never took me out of the story, it made it feel more grounded and real. I also loved that the book was short. It told it's story and then it stopped. It never dragged or wasted time. I love brevity, what can I say! I also really enjoyed that there was lots of cross-generational relationships - teenagers, parents, grandparents - because sometimes YA feels like a bizarre teen-only world.<br /><br />I'm giving this 4 stars because I don't think it was my perfect book. I think some of Marin's reactions to things were overly angsty and that there weren't many powerful moments. I said this is the type of book I want to write because it felt like something that Nina LaCour poured herself into, something subtle and strong, a message she wanted to share. It isn't a new favourite for me, but I appreciated it lots.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1383087927634871731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1982073723" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1982073723" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1982073723?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-ff">lgbtq-ff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1982073723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6445122059102628273">Do you ever think about a book and then wonder what the last person who also read it and <b>related to it</b> was doing or if they were okay?<br/><br/>Because right now I want to write something but I honestly don't know what to say. My thoughts are lying face down on the floor with passion and I just wish someone could put a blanket over them and tell them they're fine. And I swear it's like every book makes me sad in a different way but really...it’s all the same. So yeah. I guess I'm just going to keep arrang</span>
  <span id="freeText6445122059102628273" style="display:none">Do you ever think about a book and then wonder what the last person who also read it and <b>related to it</b> was doing or if they were okay?<br><br>Because right now I want to write something but I honestly don't know what to say. My thoughts are lying face down on the floor with passion and I just wish someone could put a blanket over them and tell them they're fine. And I swear it's like every book makes me sad in a different way but really...it’s all the same. So yeah. I guess I'm just going to keep arranging words until something slips out and everyone claps and someone <i>feels</i> something?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I was okay just a moment ago. I will learn how to be okay again.”</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496098038i/22881869._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="http://czrenys.tumblr.com/post/159803703270/read-in-2017-we-are-okay-by-nina-lacour" rel="nofollow noopener">(x)</a><br><br>This book was so full of <b>sadness</b> and<b> loneliness</b> that it might as well have been made of it. <br><br>You're reading and your heart feels like someone is crushing it so slowly with a combine harvester and you just want to lay your head down on a soft bread roll and maybe just be quiet for a bit. You're reading and lying on your side and a little tear trickles into your ear (which is the most tragic of all eye moisture) because you're both sad and dramatic and listening to <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UKtyJeNpcT4" rel="nofollow noopener">this song</a> and thinking that <b>your heart would actually envelop Marin in blankets if it had arms or blankets.</b><br><br>It goes like this:<br><br>Marin's story starts and you know something tragic has happened and she's left everything behind but you don't know the whys or the hows. You guess maybe it has something to do with her <b>grandfather</b> and the things left unspoken and unanswered (like the room where she never sat foot and the picture he "<i>couldn't</i>" find). Or maybe it was <b>Mabel</b> and somewhere between them walking to the beach in sweats with a blanket and alcohol and sitting on the shore kissing and the three thousand miles she traveled to see her...something went terribly wrong.<br><br>See at this point, you <i>don't</i> really know Marin's story, but something about her words and feelings resonates with you so accurately, so intimately. There's no tangible plot yet but still... it feels as if someone has dipped their finger in a lake of you and made a ripple that goes on and on and on.<br><br> <b>Your understand her kind of lonely.</b><br><br>The kind of lonely that doesn’t depend on your surroundings, that doesn’t give a shit about the 85 unanswered messages from people who genuinely love and care about you, that is engrained so deep in your soul it’s like you’re permeable and your own skin can’t protect you from it.<br><br>The kind of lonely that just makes you want to hide inside yourself more, reminding you that you’re just an insignificant blip in the infinite structure of the universe, brought into this physical reality when you wish you could just exist fleshlessly in your head so they can’t see you and you can’t let them down.<br><br><b>You understand her kind of sad.</b><br><br>The kind of sad where it’s not enough to feel sad, you have to feel guilty for feeling sad because you feel as if you’re manipulating the people around you by being sad. You’re constantly berating yourself for making a separate physical entity stop the process of their life just to make sure your bricks were still up in a wall. You’re constantly afraid that you’re being too sad, too loudly, too obviously, that you have dug yourself into a bottomless hole of self-pity and the walls are too high to see anyone else’s problems but your own and you're so terrified it's going to ruin your relationship with everyone.<br><br>The kind of sad that is just not fair because you haven't earned it—when your life is in an objectively good place but then it all comes back at once and there is no escape—you have fallen back again into a destructive mindset and you're trying so hard but it keeps pulling you back in and you feel as if you're losing your grip on yourself and you're just going to keep shrinking until you can barely feel yourself there anymore.<br><br>And something about all of these things combined still makes me feel dangerously close to tears.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I thought that it was more likely the opposite. I must have shut grief out. Found it in books. Cried over fiction instead of the truth. The truth was unconfined, unadorned. There was no poetic language to it, no yellow butterflies, no epic floods. There wasn’t a town trapped underwater or generations of men with the same name destined to make the same mistakes. The truth was vast enough to drown in.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>But <b>what this book tells you is this:</b> you will be okay. <br><br>That loneliness in the moment is no guarantee of loneliness in the future. That feelings are transient and situations change and we just need to get through this rough patch to the place where things are better. That you can be content and happy but little twinges of sadness will always seep in and it’s <i>okay</i>, because happiness has never been a fixed point in one’s life and life is just a series of challenges and ups and downs and you must learn to go with the flow.<br><br>That it can be hard and it's another day in the bathroom stall, sobbing for five minutes. Another day of giving in to depression naps in the middle of the day, another day of being unable to graduate from under your duvet. <br><br>But then <b>happy shows up.</b> <br><br>And it’s your cat purring on your lap, it’s curling up on the couch with a book, it’s a girl smiling at you on the train, its a small unexpected kindness from a stranger, it's a rainy night and blankets and your soul is warm, it’s a lovely comment a stranger left on your review, it’s some stupid meme your friend sent you because it reminded them of you, it’s finding money in your jeans pockets, it's in coffee shops and bookstores and sunsets and your grandmother's embrace, it’s your best friend coming home from college in two weeks, it’s your otp being canon and an uploaded new chapter of your favorite webcomic.<br><br>Happy <i>will</i> show up. And you will learn to find it even if it’s not where you expected it.<br><br><b>And you will be okay.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“it’s a dark place, not knowing. It’s difficult to surrender to. But I guess it’s where we live most of the time. I guess it’s where we all live, so maybe it doesn’t have to be so lonely. Maybe I can settle into it, cozy up to it, make a home inside uncertainty.”</i>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_2060927294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2060927294" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2060927294?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-audiobook">x-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=gorgeous-writing">gorgeous-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=elle-recs-list">elle-recs-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2018">y-out2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2018">z-faves2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060927294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7231088883482703961"><i>We Are Okay</i> is a book about learning the people you used to love were something beyond what you believed them to be. It is a book about learning to move on. It is a book about <u>learning to be with yourself and be with your grief</u>. It is also a book about loneliness, deep and profound loneliness, cloying and suffocating. <br/><br/>In clearer terms, this is a book about Marin, a girl who has lost her grandfather, and in doing so, pushed away her former best friend, Mabel. So when Mabel comes to town, Marin do</span>
  <span id="freeText7231088883482703961" style="display:none"><i>We Are Okay</i> is a book about learning the people you used to love were something beyond what you believed them to be. It is a book about learning to move on. It is a book about <u>learning to be with yourself and be with your grief</u>. It is also a book about loneliness, deep and profound loneliness, cloying and suffocating. <br /><br />In clearer terms, this is a book about Marin, a girl who has lost her grandfather, and in doing so, pushed away her former best friend, Mabel. So when Mabel comes to town, Marin does not know what to do with the memories. Marin at once does not want Mabel here, regrets her being here, but also desperately wants Mabel to love her. She has walls up and she wants them down, but she is too terrified for them to ever come down. Marin has lost everything, including Mabel, her best friend and her maybe-something-more. <br /><br />But it’s not a romance between Marin and Mabel. That is what is perhaps the saddest part. I once saw Nina LaCour talk live about this book, and she said something that perfectly sums up what is so arresting about this book: being queer and in love with your best friend is different than being straight and in love with your best friend. One is an experience in first love, and one is also that, but with an added experience of fear – not of rejection but of disgust. We do not want to hurt our best friends by loving them. We have learned to be ashamed of love and we carry that with us, through thick and through thin. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“If only I had something to take the edge off the loneliness. If only lonely were a more accurate word. It should sound much less pretty.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Loneliness is not a queer-only experience, not by any means; that would not be a fair claim. But <b>being queer is a loneliness experience</b>. We are all, in our own ways, not a part of the norm, not a part of the life others are allowed. We find our own lives in the cracks and spaces. (“I could say the night felt magical, but that would be embellishment - that would be romanticization. What it actually felt like was life,” Marin says of her first and only date with Mabel.) And in the wake of losing a grandfather, of losing the only person she has ever been raised by, Marin has found herself caught in a trap of being alone; she cannot rekindle a friendship with Mabel, because their history screams too loud. <br /><br />None of this is stated in <i>We Are Okay</i>, but the idea of loneliness is perhaps the most consistent fact of the story; whether alone or with Mabel, Marin is always lonely. She is always lonely, until she and Mabel finally discuss and unpack their history, and move on to a future where they can both heal, as friends if not as lovers.<br /><br /><i>We Are Okay</i> is not an action-packed story, and it is not in your face, and it will not make you scream at One Specific Significant Line. It is a book to feel, a book to hurt, and a book to heal. I’ve been trying to understand for months how I felt about this book because I think sitting on something like this is absolutely essential. <i>We Are Okay</i> is an incredibly slow, an incredibly quiet, an incredibly subtle story, but thinking back on my experience reading it two years ago, I feel like crying. It means the world. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7231088883482703961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1944816187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15740364763501884616">This is possibly the prettiest book I’ve held in my hands. As pretty as the picture looks, the hardcover is twice as lovely. <br/><br/>So I’m definitely glad I enjoyed the story, because otherwise I would have felt morally obliged to donate the book. <br/><br/>Nina LaCour doesn’t write; she paints. Delicately and purposefully. Her words are colors that blend into one another to create a magnificent landscape. <br/><br/>This is a book about family, first love, grief and solitude. Before she began college, Marin lived with her</span>
  <span id="freeText15740364763501884616" style="display:none">This is possibly the prettiest book I’ve held in my hands. As pretty as the picture looks, the hardcover is twice as lovely. <br /><br />So I’m definitely glad I enjoyed the story, because otherwise I would have felt morally obliged to donate the book. <br /><br />Nina LaCour doesn’t write; she paints. Delicately and purposefully. Her words are colors that blend into one another to create a magnificent landscape. <br /><br />This is a book about family, first love, grief and solitude. Before she began college, Marin lived with her grandfather. They weren’t close – so many secrets between them – but they had each other, which was more than Marin could have wished for.<br /><br />But one day, her grandpa dies unexpectedly and Marin is alone in the world again, for the second time since her mother died. Mabel is three thousand miles away, with a new boyfriend, and Marin isn’t ready to open up to anyone.<br /><br />I could feel Marin’s fragility and loneliness in every word. I can’t imagine what it must be like to be without family. It can destroy a person. Tear them to shreds.<br /><br />Fortunately, sensing something is wrong with her friend and former girlfriend, Mabel visits Marin at college for three days. Will this encourage her to talk about her past and feelings?<br /><br />If I had to choose one word to describe this story, I would say it’s ‘‘quiet.’’ Tranquil. Melancholic, even. You must know this is unlike those novels that have dozens of events which form a plot. It’s not about going from point A to point B; it’s about digging up point A and putting its pieces back together. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1919230727" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1919230727" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1919230727?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=pink-covers">pink-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1919230727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4549501458412163099"><i>“The trouble with denial is that when the truth comes, you aren’t ready.”</i><br/><br/>Marin hasn’t spoken to anyone from her old life since the day she left everything behind. No one knows the truth about those final weeks. Not even her best friend, Mabel. But even thousands of miles away from the California coast, at college in New York, Marin still feels the pull of the life and tragedy she’s tried to outrun. Now, months later, alone in an emptied dorm for winter break, Marin waits. Mabel is coming to visi</span>
  <span id="freeText4549501458412163099" style="display:none"><i>“The trouble with denial is that when the truth comes, you aren’t ready.”</i><br><br>Marin hasn’t spoken to anyone from her old life since the day she left everything behind. No one knows the truth about those final weeks. Not even her best friend, Mabel. But even thousands of miles away from the California coast, at college in New York, Marin still feels the pull of the life and tragedy she’s tried to outrun. Now, months later, alone in an emptied dorm for winter break, Marin waits. Mabel is coming to visit, and Marin will be forced to face everything that’s been left unsaid and finally confront the loneliness that has made a home in her heart.<br><br><i>“If our past selves got a glimpse of us now, what would they make of us?”</i><br><br>This book came so unexpectedly into my life, but I'm eternally grateful that it did so. There's simply so much to love about <b>We Are Okay</b> that I'm feeling slightly overwhelmed writing this, but thankfully lists exist for me to break it down point by point:<br><br>• We have a switching narrative between the past and future, which adds tremendously to the ongoing intrigue. Usually with books that have a similar structure, I struggle connecting with either the past or the present but that was not the case with <b>We Are Okay</b>. Far from it, actually. I kept switching my love for the chapters set in the past and those set in the present. <br>• The author gets so many things right. From leaving your home and friends and childhood behind, to tackling loneliness, grief, friendship, f/f love, bisexuality, heartbreak, and talking about books and paintings, positive adult figures, and so much more. But I especially want to address how Marin’s broken longing felt so palpable. I could virtually feel her grief coming off the page, which is by no means an easy feat to achieve in writing.<br>• Speaking of, LaCour's words blew me off the page. I just loved how certain scenes drew a perfectly fitting picture in my mind.<br><br>Exhibit A:<br><br><i>“She leans over our table and turns the sign in the window so that it says CLOSED on the outside. But on our side, perfectly positioned between Mabel’s place and mine, it says OPEN. If this were a short story, it would mean something.”</i><br><br>I had to laugh at how witty that passage was.<br><br>And then hiding my smile at this gentle and still scene following at nighttime:<br><br><i>“So I turn over and find Mabel closer to me than I’d realized. I wait a minute there to see if she’ll move away, but she doesn’t. I wrap my arm around her waist, and she relaxes into me. My head nestles in the curve behind her neck; my knees pull up to fit the space behind hers.<br>She might be asleep. I’ll only stay here for a couple of minutes. Only until I thaw completely. Until it’s enough to remind me what it feels like to be close to another person, enough to last me for another span of months. I breathe her in. Tell myself I need to turn away.<br>Soon. But not yet.<br>“Don’t disappear again,” she says. “Okay?”<br>Her hair is soft against my face.<br>“Promise me.”<br>“I promise.”</i><br><br>My heart. These two have my heart.<br><br>• The summer chapters are set in San Francisco, mainly at the beach, which is one of my all-time favorite locations.<br><br><i>“Tourists descended onto our beach, sat in our usual places, so we borrowed Ana’s car and crossed the Golden Gate to find a tiny piece of ocean to have for ourselves. We ate fish-and-chips in a dark pub that belonged in a different country, and we collected beach glass instead of shells, and we kissed in the redwoods, we kissed in the water, we kissed in movie theaters all over the city during matinees and late-night showings. We kissed in bookstores and record stores and dressing rooms. We kissed outside of the Lexington because we were too young to get in. We looked inside its doors at all the women there with short hair and long hair, lipstick and tattoos, tight dresses and tight jeans, button-ups and camisoles, and we pictured ourselves among them.”</i><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487842014ra/22055931.gif" width="500" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>• And since Marin’s from San Francisco but moved to NYC for college, the winter chapters set for the perfectly gloomy and quiet atmosphere. And as this books mentions, <i>“It was quiet, maybe, but it wasn’t simple.”</i><br>• I loved the attention paid to details. You could tell how much the story meant to the author just by little things such as the names of the girls:<br><br><i>“Just different enough,” I said.<br>“As usual.”<br>Since we’d met, we had a thing for our names’ symmetry. An M followed by a vowel, then a consonant, then a vowel, then a consonant. We thought it was important. We thought it must have meant something. Like a similar feeling must have passed through our mothers as they named us. Like destiny was at work already. We may have been in different countries, but it was only a matter of time before we would collide into each other.”</i><br><br>• And now that I've successfully circled back to my favorites, I have to talk about how stunningly earnest their relationship felt. We get to see them through all the stages: from strangers to friends to lovers to something more to something undefinable and then... And then going back and forth until they find their footing. It was everything I wanted and more. They're so good for one another.<br>• Like I wrote in my review for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1848238968" rel="nofollow noopener">Queens of Geek</a>, I live for books that write about girls. Girls supporting girls. Girls loving girls. Girls, girls, girls!!! And so this book fulfilled my heart while reading about Marin's remarkable roommate and compassionate new boss and noteworthy best friend.<br><br><i>“I look at her. I wish her everything good. A friendly cab driver and short lines through security. A flight with no turbulence and an empty seat next to her. A beautiful Christmas. I wish her more happiness than can fit in a person. I wish her the kind of happiness that spills over.”</i><br><br>This is still one of the kindest things I’ve ever read. My eyes are burning again.<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487842014i/22055932.jpg" width="475" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>• Side note: the amount of times my eyes teared up while reading was low-key alarming. But it was like I couldn't help it, especially towards the end. Like Marin said, <i>“I was crying, trying not to cry.”</i> <b>We Are Okay</b> is tragic and hopeful and morose and every adjective in the world that will help encompass the beauty of this story.<br>• And last but not least, I delighted in the fact that the families played such a big part in this book. Specifically centering on Mabel's Mexican-American family and how fervently they welcomed Marin with open arms. Ana and Javier are two of the kindest souls and made my heart swell more than once with their words and actions.<br><br>All in all: I'm beyond grateful that I picked this up on a whim because I don't think I'll find anything like it soon. But I know that I'll look forward to any of Nina LaCour's future works to come out.<br><br>P.S. <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D5drYkLiLI8" rel="nofollow noopener">This song</a> felt really fitting for the mood this story is conveying (since it also mentions summertime and being seventeen and drinking whiskey). I listened to it on repeat until, to paraphrase this book, its sound turned to nothing.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519483221i/25115431.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519483221i/25115431.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519483221i/25115431.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519483221i/25115431.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519483221i/25115431.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <em>Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</em>
</i> <strong>We Are Okay</strong>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!</i><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0525425896/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=0525425896&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=9af87aa9fcfbc91c082f279dfb5d8ebb" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487842014i/22055933.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">This review and more can be found on my blog.</a></span>

<div id="review_2735846034" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2735846034" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2735846034?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780735232013" href="/book/show/34281321-we-are-okay">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2735846034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8608420449989549517">lets talk about grief. and how it affects everyone in different ways. its can slowly creep up on you. it can hit you suddenly and with great intensity. and sometimes its always present, making itself comfortable in your loneliness. its one of those emotions that is difficult to express and, because of that, i applaud this story. grief and loneliness are not pretty feelings, but this novel handles them will care and authenticity. and while the writing in this story is beautiful, grief can be a ve</span>
  <span id="freeText8608420449989549517" style="display:none">lets talk about grief. and how it affects everyone in different ways. its can slowly creep up on you. it can hit you suddenly and with great intensity. and sometimes its always present, making itself comfortable in your loneliness. its one of those emotions that is difficult to express and, because of that, i applaud this story. grief and loneliness are not pretty feelings, but this novel handles them will care and authenticity. and while the writing in this story is beautiful, grief can be a very ugly thing and i appreciate how this story shows that. ugliness and all. this story is so human and its very refreshing to read. <br /><br />the main reason i didnt round up my rating, which i normally do, is because this didnt quite impact me as much as i was hoping. for being such a real and heavy story, i felt a little emotionally distant from it. due to the content matter, i believe this is the kind of story will impact people in different ways depending on whats going on in the readers life. for me, grief isnt something i have experienced a lot lately. i have no doubt that if i were to pick this up at a different point in time, this story would resonate with me more profoundly. <br /><br />overall, this is a such a genuine and tender story about grief, loneliness, and one girls desire to overcome them via the bonds of friends and family. a must read for those needing a little extra support, love and a gentle reminder that you are not alone. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8608420449989549517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3027018769" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3027018769" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3027018769?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780735232013" href="/book/show/34281321-we-are-okay">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3027018769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14836709179326405495"><i>”I wonder if there’s a secret current that connects people who have lost something. Not in the way that everyone loses something, but in the way that undoes your life, undoes your self, so that when you look at your face it isn’t yours anymore.”</i><br/><br/>This book was one of the most beautiful books I ever read. Not only because the writing style is amazing but also because there is so much truth in it. The truth can be beautiful, it can be bittersweet, it can be painful and excruciating, it can hurt you </span>
  <span id="freeText14836709179326405495" style="display:none"><i>”I wonder if there’s a secret current that connects people who have lost something. Not in the way that everyone loses something, but in the way that undoes your life, undoes your self, so that when you look at your face it isn’t yours anymore.”</i><br /><br />This book was one of the most beautiful books I ever read. Not only because the writing style is amazing but also because there is so much truth in it. The truth can be beautiful, it can be bittersweet, it can be painful and excruciating, it can hurt you but it can also give you hope. The truth of <b>“We Are Okay”</b>? It does all those things and even more. <br /><br /><i>”No one will know if you stay in bed all day. No one will know if you wear the same sweatpants for the entire month, if you eat every meal in front of television shows and use T-shirts as napkins. Go ahead and listen to that same song on repeat until its sound turns to nothing and you sleep the winter away.”</i><br /><br />There’s a sadness in this book, on every page, in every single line. It seeps from the pages, it’s a tangible and breathing thing. It makes it hard to pick up the book and it stays throughout the entire story. A silent and looming companion, something to be afraid of but also something that keeps you going, something that accompanies you, for better or for worse. There were so many things I could relate to and I think my personal experiences made up a big part of the story’s appeal. <br /><br /><i>”I’m just afraid that one day something’s going to catch me by surprise. Stale coffee. Squares of American cheese. Hard tomatoes, so unripe they’re white in the center. The most innocent things can call back the most terrible.”</i><br /><br />How can anyone who hasn’t gone through loss even comprehend how hard it is to remain a living, functioning and acting part of this world? The answer is simple: They can’t. Grief is something that changes you, it turns and twists you, you might look the same on the outside but on the inside you’re shaken to your core. Once grief found you, it leaves its mark and it’s something you carry with you for the rest of your life. You can’t get rid of it and you recognize it in people that made the same experiences.<br /><br /><i>”But I know that there’s a difference between how I used to understand things and how I do now. I used to cry over a story and then close the book, and it all would be over. Now everything resonates, sticks like a splinter, festers.”</i><br /><br />I don’t know about you, but I’m always glad for the people who never experienced such a profound loss. They still have some sort of innocence to them; they’ve never been shattered like that and don’t have to try to fit together the pieces of a puzzle they didn’t even know existed. It’s not easy to come back from this kind of grief and it doesn’t only take away your innocence, it also steals your youth. <br /><br /><i>”In the kitchen, I put a pot of water on the stove. Before the water reaches a boil, he will be here. I dropped pasta in and set the timer. Before the then minutes are up. I melted some butter. I wasn’t hungry, but I would eat it anyway, and by the time I was done, he would walk through the door and call out my name.”</i><br /><br />*sighs* How I could relate to this part of the book. The waiting, the hoping that her grandfather would turn up. The ingrained <b>KNOWING</b> that he wouldn’t. That utter and deafening sense that something is wrong but you can’t do anything to make it right. You’re helpless, desperate and frantic and you just don’t know what to do. Until, well, until someone eventually confirms your biggest fears. Until someone shatters your world forever.<br /><br /><i>”And Hannah kept saving me. She saved me with never asking questions, with instead reading to me about bees and botany and evolution. She saved me with clothes she loaned me and never took back. She saved me with seats next to her in the dining hall, with quick evasions when people asked me questions I couldn’t answer, with chapters read aloud and forced trips off campus and rides to the grocery store and a pair of winter boots.”</i><br /><br />But thankfully there are people like Hannah out there. People that watch out for you, that don’t turn away from you but embrace you with all your shattered parts. I’m pretty sure Hannah might have experienced loss too because she stuck with Marin and in my experience only people that went through it will react like that. The others? Well, those who are fortunate will have never experienced anything like it, so they’ll say how sorry they are, they’ll try to cheer you up, but when you fall into that black and endless rabbit hole of grief. Well, they’ll eventually lose interest after a few days or weeks (if you’re lucky) and then move on. Without you…<br /><br />It took Marin months to speak about her loss; it took me an entire year to open up and to speak about mine. A year that changed me forever, a year I’ll never get back. I really wish I would have had this book when I was seventeen and I hope and pray that everyone who experiences the very same thing will stumble upon it. That they’ll find solace and hope in Nina LaCour’s words and that they’ll eventually find the strength to move on. Because the truth is: Life is merciless and it doesn’t pause for the living.<br /><br />If I learned anything then it’s this and that you’ve to live your life like there will be no tomorrow.<br />Make your experiences, don’t regret anything, recognize your loss, stay true to yourself, keep on fighting, keep living, because it’s worth it. Life is so worth it and you only have one chance! Make it count! ;-)<br /><br />This said, I love this book with all my heart and I’ll recommend it to everyone who ever experienced loss! This, this is your book! Your voice! Your thoughts on paper! Read it and heal! &lt;3<br /><br /><i>"Say yes."</i><br /><br />___________________________<br /><br />A lot of my friends read this book and they all gave it a stellar rating, so I’m pretty curious if I’ll like it too. <br /><br />From what I could glean from the updates the title seems to be the complete opposite of what it claims and naturally this only caused me to be even more intrigued. <br /><br /><b>“We are okay.”</b> <s>Until we’re not</s><br /><br />Let’s find out if this is one of those stories…</span>
  <a data-text-id="14836709179326405495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1947034818" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1947034818" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1947034818?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=beautifully-written">beautifully-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=3-and-a-half-stars">3-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1947034818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16851667704597547591">The person who will like this book is a very particular one.<br/><br/>If you don’t like character-driven stuff, STAY FAR AWAY FROM THIS BOOK. No, seriously. Leave this review right now, even. There is not even a question of you possibly liking this book. SO GET OUT OF HERE, OKAY?<br/><br/>Just kidding. You can stay if you want. But only if it’s for my charming personality and not for a potential recommendation.<br/><br/>Okay. Now I am going to try to make A Point that is perched on a very thin line. And I will almost certain</span>
  <span id="freeText16851667704597547591" style="display:none">The person who will like this book is a very particular one.<br /><br />If you don’t like character-driven stuff, STAY FAR AWAY FROM THIS BOOK. No, seriously. Leave this review right now, even. There is not even a question of you possibly liking this book. SO GET OUT OF HERE, OKAY?<br /><br />Just kidding. You can stay if you want. But only if it’s for my charming personality and not for a potential recommendation.<br /><br />Okay. Now I am going to try to make A Point that is perched on a very thin line. And I will almost certainly fail ini this endeavor.<br /><br />As someone who writes a lot of negative reviews, I understand that people have varying opinions on books. Duh. That’s, like, part of what makes this whole reviewing thing fun. And even with the books I love most, I try to never be like, “What the hell!!!! It’s illegal for you to give this one star!!!”<br /><br />Except for Alice’s Adventures in Wonderland. Because I’m currently thirty-seven months away from achieving the “sole Goodreads admin” phase of my eighteen-step world domination program, and when that happens it <i>literally will</i> be impossible for you to give one star to the greatest book of all time.<br /><br />If you think about it, I’m really just being considerate.<br /><br />But back to this point I’m procrastinating.<br /><br />Here’s what I’m trying to sidestep, but will eventually just have to come out and say in some way, shape, or form, and I may as well do so succinctly and now:<br /><br />If you don’t like this book, I think you’re wrong.<br /><br />The major complaint I’ve seen about it is that it’s “boring.” And I get that. And like, I’m really sorry, but depression is not exactly a day trip to the amusement park. So it’s not going to rank alongside heists and nefarious plotting and research montages in terms of top-five most entertaining storylines.<br /><br /><i>But that doesn’t mean it’s not an important book.</i><br /><br />If you don’t want to read a depiction of mourning and depression and a semi-realistically-staged healing process, that’s fair - so just STAY AWAY. Don’t blame the book for being boring. It’s not fun to be depressed.<br /><br />There were bits of the overall depiction that I didn’t like. Things that felt too convenient, or dramatic, or cheesy. There was a strange twist I never understood, and the relationship at the core of the text confused me to no end, and there was maybe a little too much hope. (Depression isn’t there and gone.)<br /><br />But generally, this is one of the better renditions of depression I’ve seen in YA. It’s also so f*cking good at discussing some of the difficulties of going to college. It captures that initial loneliness.<br /><br />(Wow. I’m really making myself excited to start all over again when I start at a whole new college at the end of the summer. Yay, transferring.)<br /><br />Jesus Christ I wish I had a half star. This book was <i>not</i> a three star read, but I’m equally opposed to giving it four, goddamn it.<br /><br />Anyway. I feel preach-y and I hate myself for it and I want to shut up. So I’m just going to say this book is also beautifully written and then throw in some quotes and leave.<br /><br />Bottom line: Only read it if you know what you’re getting into. Because if you two-star it for being boring after reading this review, I get to pinch you.<br /><br />Read the fine print.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>SOME QUOTES</b><br /><br />“I wish you more happiness than can fit in a person.”<br /><br />“I could say the night felt magical, but that would be embellishment. <br />That would be romanticization.<br />What it actually felt like was life.” <br /><br />“We were nostalgic for a time that wasn't yet over.” <br /><br />“If only I had something to take the edge off the loneliness. If only lonely were a more accurate word. It should sound much less pretty.” </span>
  <a data-text-id="16851667704597547591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13882657306477464352">[4.5 stars] I'm crying buckets. I haven't cried this much over a book since I finished reading A Court of Wings and Ruin. This book was stunning. Absolutely stunning. I felt every single word. Some of them were just outright painful, but I was connected, grieving alongside Marin.<br/><br/>It is an incredible story about a girl who's coming to terms with the death of her grandfather and her losses in life, which she's experienced so much of so young. Such a short book, but so beautifully impactful.</span>

<div id="review_1916168303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1916168303" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1916168303?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1916168303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7190918819091467944">Update -- This is $2.99 today as a kindle download -- (read other reviews) -- its not for everyone -- but it was for me. I haven't given away my hard copy -I love how it feels in my hand -- its funny how my mind works - If this were a $1.99 today --(instead of $2.99) -- I might buy it --then finally give my physical copy away. Gotta clear out books once in awhile! <br/><br/>Point is -- if you THINK this book is for YOU -- it probably is!!!! I saw 'low' reviews 'before' I read it --yet I still knew I wante</span>
  <span id="freeText7190918819091467944" style="display:none">Update -- This is $2.99 today as a kindle download -- (read other reviews) -- its not for everyone -- but it was for me. I haven't given away my hard copy -I love how it feels in my hand -- its funny how my mind works - If this were a $1.99 today --(instead of $2.99) -- I might buy it --then finally give my physical copy away. Gotta clear out books once in awhile! <br /><br />Point is -- if you THINK this book is for YOU -- it probably is!!!! I saw 'low' reviews 'before' I read it --yet I still knew I wanted to read it. I loved it!! sooooooooooo much feeling --things to think about in this little pint size book!<br /><br />Morning Thursday greetings!!! xox<br /><br /><br /><br />I was drawn to this book from the first time I saw it. Soon after, I saw several 'low' . I was still curious. <br /><br />I knew parts of this book took place in the SF Bay Area... parts in New York....plus I had read that the author, Nina LaCour, lives in Oakland, Ca. I was 'jazzed'. How bad could this book be? NOT BAD AT ALL FOR ME!!!! I LOVE LOVE LOVE THIS BOOK!!!!<br /><br />I read this book slow over 3 days. ----The story takes place over 3 days too! <br /><br />It's a tiny book. It could be read in one or two hours, but that's not how I read it. I knew early on that I didn't want to say goodbye to MARIN!!! I didn't want to leave her... I just wanted to be there - with this young girl as much as possible. I wanted to tell her ---"I understand the loneliness- the grief - the fears - the emptiness. I related to her and her situation. <br />THIS STORY BROUGHT UP PAST MEMORIES for me.....<br /> .....of the summer between my Senior Year in High School and College<br /> .....of living alone with only my mother -passing each other like distant roommates.<br /> ......years of living in an apt. -- threadbare- just my mother and I.<br /> ......I thought of David Vann's book, "Aquarium", ... even though the stories are different. This book brought back feelings I had from that powerful book, too.<br /> ......I remembered a time - living in Oakland - around the time Martin Luther King died...of not knowing where my mother was for a couple of days - scared and worried. <br /> ......I thought about my grandparents and their pawnshop store on Broadway Ave. in Oakland. I thought about my private time with my 'Gramps' before he died. I was only 7 when he died of a stroke - two years after my dad died of a heart attack. <br /> ......I thought about all the many kids that grow up with with only 1 caretaker-adult. ( especially an only child). <br /> ......I also thought of our own older daughter. ( a sweet happy memory). There was reference to the play "The Turning of the Screw", in "We Are Okay". <br />Our daughter played the leading female role at the San Jose Rep. She was 12 years old. It was her first equity performance -- phenomenal show -- performances were extended beyond the standard 6 week run. <br /> ........I 'still' wish I didn't have to say goodbye to Marin. I like Mabel too!! <br /><br />To me .... this is close to a perfect book! It may not be for everyone- but for some of us it allows our souls to sing!!!<br /><br /> One excerpt:<br /> "It was a summer of trying not to think too deeply. A summer of pretending that the end wasn't coming. A summer I got lost in time, when I rarely knew what day it was, rarely cared about the hour. A summer so bright and warm it made me believe the heat would linger, that there would always be more days, that blood on handkerchiefs was an exercise in stain removal and not a sign of oblivion". <br /><br />I've already been reading pages again. I absolutely treasure this book!!!!!!<br /><br />Even the 'acknowledgments' .... the touching sharing by author Nina LaCour moved me - and warmed me all over!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7190918819091467944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1942439030" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1942439030" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1942439030?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780735232013" href="/book/show/34281321-we-are-okay">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1942439030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5138857726123957408"><i>“If only lonely were a more accurate word. It should sound much less pretty.”</i><br/><br/>There are books that roar and scream and radiate power. This is not one of those books. It is a book that shows ultimate strength in its tranquillity. <i>We Are Okay</i> may be a quiet book, but its force will tear you apart and put you back together again. It will give room to your grief, then stroke your hair, hug you tightly and warm your heart piece by piece.<br/><br/>By the first page, I was already lost between the pages of this b</span>
  <span id="freeText5138857726123957408" style="display:none"><i>“If only lonely were a more accurate word. It should sound much less pretty.”</i><br /><br />There are books that roar and scream and radiate power. This is not one of those books. It is a book that shows ultimate strength in its tranquillity. <i>We Are Okay</i> may be a quiet book, but its force will tear you apart and put you back together again. It will give room to your grief, then stroke your hair, hug you tightly and warm your heart piece by piece.<br /><br />By the first page, I was already lost between the pages of this book. By page sixty I had nearly burst into tears in public three times. I recommend you do not read this on public transport. But I could not put it down. I savoured every single sentence, every word. This book tells the story of loss, grief, and loneliness. It resonated deeply with me, and more than once I felt completely understood. The author knows how to define different kinds of silence: That between two people who have lost each other and try to find their way back to being an "us", a "we". The silence of a heart too hurt to remember the past. The silence of a warm fireplace and snow falling outside. Nina LaCour knows about growing up, about nostalgia for something that has not yet passed and, more importantly, she knows how to put these feelings into words that make you feel them, too.<br /><br />She also knows that your sexuality is not the only important thing about you as a person. That it is not the only story you have to tell.<br /><br />I think I fell a little bit in love with this book.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5138857726123957408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2361216860" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2361216860" />
    <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks"><img alt="BernLuvsBooks " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585010050p2/3087404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2361216860?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40003466-we-are-okay">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2361216860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14964886939975861849"><b> <i> "Life is paper thin and fragile. Any sudden change could rip it wide-open." </i></b> <br/><br/>A short, easy read (I read it in a few hours in 1 sitting) about loneliness, heartbreak & eventual healing. It's slow paced - there isn't any real action in the plot. It's really centered around emotion - Marin's feelings which become clearer to us as we read, allowing us to learn her truths. <br/><br/>I enjoyed the story for what it was but I personally wasn't blown away by it. There were parts that dragged a bit for me and wi</span>
  <span id="freeText14964886939975861849" style="display:none"><b> <i> "Life is paper thin and fragile. Any sudden change could rip it wide-open." </i></b> <br /><br />A short, easy read (I read it in a few hours in 1 sitting) about loneliness, heartbreak &amp; eventual healing. It's slow paced - there isn't any real action in the plot. It's really centered around emotion - Marin's feelings which become clearer to us as we read, allowing us to learn her truths. <br /><br />I enjoyed the story for what it was but I personally wasn't blown away by it. There were parts that dragged a bit for me and with it being such a quick/short read I didn't expect that. The end though - I really enjoyed it. <b>There was so much love, raw emotion &amp; hope within those last few pages.</b> I just didn't enjoy the entire book as much as I did those last few pages making this one a 3.5 star read for me. It wasn't bad. It wasn't great. It was a book I enjoyed, just not one I think I will remember with much detail over time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14964886939975861849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2855768524" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2855768524" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2855768524?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2855768524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1577598488957338510">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>"I wonder if there's a secret current that connects people who have lost something. Not in the way that everyone loses something, but in the way that undoes your life, undoes your self, so that when you look at your face it isn't yours anymore."<br/><br/>Marin (pronounced like the county in California) was once surrounded by people who loved her. She was raised by her grandfather since her mother's death when she was young, and Marin and her best friend, Mabel, were inseparable. She even was clo</span>
  <span id="freeText1577598488957338510" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br />"I wonder if there's a secret current that connects people who have lost something. Not in the way that everyone loses something, but in the way that undoes your life, undoes your self, so that when you look at your face it isn't yours anymore."<br /><br />Marin (pronounced like the county in California) was once surrounded by people who loved her. She was raised by her grandfather since her mother's death when she was young, and Marin and her best friend, Mabel, were inseparable. She even was close to Mabel's parents, who treated her a bit like she was their own daughter.<br /><br />But Marin fled her California home in the wake of a discovery and a tragedy, and now she is poised to spend Christmas by herself in her dorm room in chilly New York. Although her roommate has helped Marin navigate the many awkward moments and uncertainties of freshman year in college, she still considers herself to be a loner, unworthy of the attention people are paying her and unsure of how to interact with people.<br /><br />What Marin is most apprehensive about during the holidays is facing Mabel, who is coming to visit from California for three days. The two haven't spoken since Mabel left for college, just before the tragedy that sent Marin running. Mabel doesn't understand what happened to her friend, and why she hasn't responded to almost all of her texts, calls, and emails. And no one understands why Marin left her old life behind.<br /><br />Marin isn't sure she's ready to share the truth with anyone, let alone Mabel. If she does, she also will have to confront her feelings, which have mostly remained hidden all this time, and she may have to accept how much things have changed. She's also afraid to let her guard down and leave her heart open, for fear that once again she might be left with nothing.<br /><br />What happened back in California that made Marin run and not look back? Why is she willing to be alone rather than share her pain, her fears, her grief with those who love her? Why would she rather be alone than try to make friends and move on with her life?<br /><br />Nina LaCour's <b>
  <i>We Are Okay</i>
</b> is nearly 250 pages long, but it packs a potent, emotional punch. This is a thought-provoking, tremendously poignant book that so deftly explored how grief and betrayal can truly destroy a person, and how when we need rescuing the most we're unwilling to let anyone help. At the same time, the book painted a fascinating picture about friendship, and how it can bring both joy and pain.<br /><br />I loved the book that LaCour wrote with David Levithan, <b>
  <i>You Know Me Well</i>
</b>, and this book cemented my admiration of the way she writes. I was a little confused by some elements of the plot and it took a while for Marin to reveal—to Mabel and to the reader—the reasons behind her actions. (I'll admit I still was unclear for longer than I should have been!) But those issues notwithstanding, this book left me a teary-eyed mess when I read it in one sitting on a flight.<br /><br />Books about friendships and how they shape us—for better or worse—always appeal to me, and <b>
  <i>We Are Okay</i>
</b> is an excellent addition to that oeuvre. Pick it up for the emotion; stay for LaCour's sensational storytelling.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2018 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html</a>. <br /><br />You can follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1577598488957338510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
